The vast majority of the reported cases are school-aged children and their parents.</p><br class=" "><br class=" "><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">Whooping cough, or pertussis, is a highly contagious respiratory tract infection. It can be spread through the air when an infected person coughs or sneezes.</p><br class=" "><br class=" "><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">The most common symptoms are cough, nasal congestion and fever. The cough can last several weeks.</p><br class=" "><br class=" "><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">"With so many respiratory illnesses currently circulating, some for which there are no treatment, we wanted to make sure that parents know that pertussis, also called whooping cough, can be treated with antibiotics if diagnosed early," said Suffolk County Health Commissioner Dr. Gregson Pigott. "Whooping cough can be very serious for infants too young to be vaccinated, which is why we are alerting both medical providers and the public that this illness is circulating."</p><br class=" "><br class=" "><div class="oLzSq QrHMO fnRUo pvsTF EhJPu vPlOC zNYgW OsTsW RMeqy daRVX ISNQ sKyCY eRftA acPPc MENS nFwaT MCnQE mEeeY SmBjI xegrY rPLsU iulOd NIuqO zzscu lzDCc aHUBM IEgzD OjMNy eQqcx SVqKB GQmdz jaoD VWDdR ONJdw vrZxD OnRTz gbbfF roDbV GPGwb oMlSS gfNzt oJhud eXZcf zhVlX "><div></div></div><br class=" "><br class=" "><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">Infants, especially when unvaccinated or not fully vaccinated, are the most likely to have severe disease or complications such as pauses in breathing, convulsions, pneumonia, disease affecting the brain, or death.</p><br class=" "><br class=" "><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">Routine vaccination against whooping cough is recommended for children and adults. Most people can recover with a course of antibiotics.</p><br class=" "><br class=" "><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">Preventative antibiotics are also available for people who are high risk and are exposed to someone infected with whooping cough.</p><br class=" "><br class=" "><p class="EkqkG IGXmU nlgHS yuUao lqtkC TjIXL aGjvy ">No hospitalizations from this outbreak of whooping cough have been reported, health officials say.</p><br class=" "><br class=" "><div class="oLzSq QrHMO fnRUo pvsTF EhJPu vPlOC zNYgW OsTsW RMeqy daRVX ISNQ sKyCY eRftA acPPc MENS nFwaT MCnQE
